<p><b>Microsoft Azure</b>, or just <b>Azure</b> (<a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/ˈæʒər, ˈeɪʒər/</a> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i>AZH-ər, AY-zhər</i></a>, <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a> also <a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/ˈæzjʊər, ˈeɪzjʊər/</a> <a href="/wiki/Help:Pronunciation_respelling_key" title="Help:Pronunciation respelling key"><i>AZ-ure, AY-zure</i></a>),<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is the <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a> platform developed by <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>. It has management, access and development of applications and services to individuals, companies, and governments through its global infrastructure. It also provides capabilities that are usually not included within other cloud platforms, including <a href="/wiki/Software_as_a_service" title="Software as a service">software as a service (SaaS)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Platform_as_a_service" title="Platform as a service">platform as a service (PaaS)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure_as_a_service" title="Infrastructure as a service">infrastructure as a service (IaaS)</a>. Microsoft Azure supports many <a href="/wiki/Programming_language" title="Programming language">programming languages</a>, tools, and frameworks, including Microsoft-specific and third-party software and systems.
</p><p>Azure was first introduced at the <a href="/wiki/Professional_Developers_Conference" title="Professional Developers Conference">Professional Developers Conference</a> (PDC) in October 2008 under the codename "Project Red Dog".<sup id="cite_ref-:1_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It was officially launched as Windows Azure in February 2010 and later renamed to Microsoft Azure on March 25, 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-anya_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anya-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-renaming_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-renaming-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Services">Services</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Services"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Microsoft Azure uses large-scale <a href="/wiki/Virtualization" title="Virtualization">virtualization</a> at Microsoft data centers worldwide and offers more than 600 services.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Microsoft Azure offers a service level agreement (SLA) that guarantees 99.9% availability for applications and data hosted on its platform, subject to specific terms and conditions outlined in the SLA documentation.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Computer_services">Computer services</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Computer services"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Virtual_machine" title="Virtual machine">Virtual machines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Infrastructure_as_a_service" title="Infrastructure as a service">infrastructure as a service</a> (IaaS), allowing users to launch general-purpose <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Windows" title="Microsoft Windows">Microsoft Windows</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> virtual machines, <a href="/wiki/Software_as_a_service" title="Software as a service">software as a service</a> (SaaS), as well as preconfigured machine images for popular software packages.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
<ul><li>Starting in 2022, these virtual machines are now powered by <a href="/wiki/Ampere_Computing" title="Ampere Computing">Ampere</a> Cloud-native processors.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Most users run Linux on Azure, some of the many <a href="/wiki/Linux_distribution" title="Linux distribution">Linux distributions</a> offered, including Microsoft's own <a href="/wiki/Linux_kernel" title="Linux kernel">Linux</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Azure_Sphere" title="Azure Sphere">Azure Sphere</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul></li>
<li>App services, <a href="/wiki/Platform_as_a_service" title="Platform as a service">platform as a service</a> (PaaS) environment, letting developers easily publish and manage websites.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Azure_Web_Apps" title="Azure Web Apps">Azure Web Sites</a> allows developers to build sites using <a href="/wiki/ASP.NET" title="ASP.NET">ASP.NET</a>, <a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">PHP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Node.js" title="Node.js">Node.js</a>, <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a>, which can be deployed using <a href="/wiki/File_Transfer_Protocol" title="File Transfer Protocol">FTP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Git" title="Git">Git</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mercurial" title="Mercurial">Mercurial</a>, <a href="/wiki/Azure_DevOps_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Azure DevOps Services">Azure DevOps</a>, or uploaded through the user portal. This feature was announced in preview form in June 2012 at the Meet Microsoft Azure event.<sup id="cite_ref-meetnew_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-meetnew-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Customers can create websites in PHP, ASP.NET, Node.js, or Python, or select from several open-source applications from a gallery to deploy. This comprises one aspect of the <a href="/wiki/Platform_as_a_service" title="Platform as a service">platform as a service</a> (PaaS) offerings for the Microsoft Azure Platform. It was renamed Web Apps in April 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-renaming_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-renaming-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Web Jobs are applications that can be deployed to an App Service environment to implement background processing that can be invoked on a schedule, on-demand, or run continuously. The Blob, Table, and Queue services can be used to communicate between Web Apps and Web Jobs and to provide state.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Azure Kubernetes Service (AKS) provides the capability to deploy production-ready <a href="/wiki/Kubernetes" title="Kubernetes">Kubernetes</a> clusters in Azure.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>In July 2023, <a href="/wiki/Digital_watermarking" title="Digital watermarking">watermarking</a> support on <a href="/wiki/Azure_Virtual_Desktop" title="Azure Virtual Desktop">Azure Virtual Desktop</a> was announced as an optional feature of <i>Screen Capture</i> to provide additional security against <a href="/wiki/Data_leakage" class="mw-redirect" title="Data leakage">data leakage</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Identity">Identity</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Identity"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>Entra ID connect is used to <a href="/wiki/Data_synchronization" title="Data synchronization">synchronize</a> on-premises directories and enable <a href="/wiki/Single_sign-on" title="Single sign-on">SSO</a> (Single Sign On).<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Entra ID B2C allows the use of consumer identity and access management in the cloud.</li>
<li>Entra Domain Services is used to join Azure virtual machines to a <a href="/wiki/Windows_domain" title="Windows domain">domain</a> without <a href="/wiki/Domain_controller_(Windows)" title="Domain controller (Windows)">domain controllers</a>.</li>
<li>Azure information protection can be used to protect <a href="/wiki/Information_sensitivity" title="Information sensitivity">sensitive information</a>.</li>
<li>Entra ID External Identities is a set of capabilities that allow organizations to collaborate with external users, including customers and partners.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On July 11, 2023, Microsoft announced the renaming of Azure AD to <i><a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Entra_ID" title="Microsoft Entra ID">Microsoft Entra ID</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The name change took place four days later.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Mobile_services">Mobile services</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Mobile services"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>Mobile Engagement collects real-time analytics that highlight users’ behavior. It also provides push notifications to mobile devices.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/HockeyApp" class="mw-redirect" title="HockeyApp">HockeyApp</a> can be used to develop, distribute, and beta-test mobile apps.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Storage_services">Storage services</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Storage services"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>Storage Services provides <a href="/wiki/REST" title="REST">REST</a> and <a href="/wiki/Software_development_kit" title="Software development kit">SDK</a> <a href="/wiki/API" title="API">APIs</a> for storing and accessing data on the cloud.</li>
<li>Table Service lets programs store structured text in <a href="/wiki/Partition_(database)" title="Partition (database)">partitioned</a> collections of entities that are accessed by the partition key and <a href="/wiki/Primary_key" title="Primary key">primary key</a>. Azure Table Service is a <a href="/wiki/NoSQL" title="NoSQL">NoSQL</a> non-relational database.</li>
<li>Blob Service allows programs to store unstructured text and binary data as <a href="/wiki/Object_storage" title="Object storage">object storage</a> blobs that can be accessed by an HTTP(S) path. Blob service also provides security mechanisms to control access to data.</li>
<li>Queue Service lets programs communicate asynchronously by message using <a href="/wiki/Message_queuing_service" title="Message queuing service">queues</a>.</li>
<li>File Service allows storing and access of data on the cloud using the REST APIs or the <a href="/wiki/SMB_protocol" class="mw-redirect" title="SMB protocol">SMB protocol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Communication_services">Communication services</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Communication services"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>Azure Communication Services offers an <a href="/wiki/Software_development_kit" title="Software development kit">SDK</a> for creating web and mobile communications applications that include <a href="/wiki/SMS" title="SMS">SMS</a>, video calling, <a href="/wiki/VOIP" class="mw-redirect" title="VOIP">VOIP</a> and <a href="/wiki/PSTN" class="mw-redirect" title="PSTN">PSTN</a> calling, and web-based chat.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Data_management">Data management</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Data management"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Azure_Data_Explorer" title="Azure Data Explorer">Azure Data Explorer</a> provides <a href="/wiki/Big_data" title="Big data">big data</a> analytics and <a href="/wiki/Data_exploration" title="Data exploration">data-exploration</a> capabilities.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Azure_Search" class="mw-redirect" title="Azure Search">Azure Search</a> provides text search and a subset of <a href="/wiki/OData" class="mw-redirect" title="OData">OData</a>'s structured filters using REST or SDK APIs.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cosmos_DB" title="Cosmos DB">Cosmos DB</a> is a <a href="/wiki/NoSQL" title="NoSQL">NoSQL</a> database service that implements a subset of the <a href="/wiki/Select_(SQL)" title="Select (SQL)">SQL SELECT</a> statement on <a href="/wiki/JSON" title="JSON">JSON</a> documents.</li>
<li>Azure Cache for Redis is a managed implementation of <a href="/wiki/Redis" title="Redis">Redis</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/StorSimple" title="StorSimple">StorSimple</a> manages storage tasks between on-premises devices and cloud storage.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Azure_SQL_Database" title="Microsoft Azure SQL Database">Azure SQL Database</a> works to create, scale, and extend applications into the cloud using <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_SQL_Server" title="Microsoft SQL Server">Microsoft SQL Server</a> technology. It also integrates with <a href="/wiki/Active_Directory" title="Active Directory">Active Directory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_System_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Microsoft System Center">Microsoft System Center</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Apache_Hadoop" title="Apache Hadoop">Hadoop</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Azure Synapse Analytics is a fully managed cloud <a href="/wiki/Data_warehouse" title="Data warehouse">data warehouse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Azure Data Factory is a <a href="/wiki/Data_integration" title="Data integration">data integration</a> service that allows creation of data-driven workflows in the cloud for orchestrating and automating data movement and data transformation.<sup id="cite_ref-adfdoc_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-adfdoc-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Azure_Data_Lake" title="Azure Data Lake">Azure Data Lake</a> is a scalable data storage and analytic service for <a href="/wiki/Big_data" title="Big data">big data</a> analytics workloads that require developers to run <a href="/wiki/Massively_parallel" title="Massively parallel">massively parallel</a> queries.</li>
<li>Azure HDInsight<sup id="cite_ref-azure.microsoft.com_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-azure.microsoft.com-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> is a big data-relevant service that deploys <a href="/wiki/Hortonworks" title="Hortonworks">Hortonworks</a> <a href="/wiki/Hadoop" class="mw-redirect" title="Hadoop">Hadoop</a> on Microsoft Azure and supports the creation of Hadoop clusters using Linux with Ubuntu.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Azure_Stream_Analytics" title="Azure Stream Analytics">Azure Stream Analytics</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Serverless_computing" title="Serverless computing">Serverless</a> scalable event-processing engine that enables users to develop and run real-time analytics on multiple streams of data from sources such as devices, sensors, websites, social media, and other applications.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Messaging">Messaging</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Messaging"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The Microsoft Azure Service Bus allows applications running on Azure premises or off-premises devices to communicate with Azure. This helps to build scalable and reliable applications in a <a href="/wiki/Service-oriented_architecture" title="Service-oriented architecture">service-oriented architecture</a> (SOA). The Azure service bus supports four different types of communication mechanisms:<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><b>Event Hubs</b>, which provides event and telemetry ingress to the cloud at a massive scale, with low <a href="/wiki/Latency_(engineering)" title="Latency (engineering)">latency</a> and high <a href="/wiki/Reliability_(computer_networking)" title="Reliability (computer networking)">reliability</a>. For example, an event hub can be used to track data from cell phones such as coordinating with a GPS in <a href="/wiki/Real-time_computing" title="Real-time computing">real time</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>Queues</b>, which allows one-directional communication. A sender application would send the message to the service bus queue and a receiver would read from the queue. Though there can be multiple readers for the queue, only one would process a single message.</li>
<li><b>Topics</b>, which provides one-directional communication using a <a href="/wiki/Publish%E2%80%93subscribe_pattern" title="Publish–subscribe pattern">subscriber pattern</a>. It is similar to a queue; however, each subscriber will receive a copy of the message sent to a Topic. Optionally, the subscriber can filter out messages based on specific criteria defined by the subscriber.</li>
<li><b>Relays</b>, which provides bi-directional communication. Unlike queues and topics, a relay does not store in-flight messages in its memory; instead, it just passes them on to the destination application.</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Media_services">Media services</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Media services"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A PaaS offering that can be used for encoding, <a href="/wiki/Content_protection" class="mw-redirect" title="Content protection">content protection</a>, streaming, or <a href="/wiki/Analytics" title="Analytics">analytics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="CDN">CDN</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: CDN"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Azure has a worldwide <a href="/wiki/Content_delivery_network" title="Content delivery network">content delivery network</a> (CDN) designed to efficiently deliver audio, video, applications, images, and other static files. It improves the performance of websites by caching static files closer to users, based on their geographic location. Users can manage the network using a REST-based HTTP API.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Azure has 118 point-of-presence locations across 100 cities worldwide (also known as Edge locations) as of January 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Developer">Developer</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Developer"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>Application Insights<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Azure_DevOps_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="Azure DevOps Services">Azure DevOps</a><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Managements">Managements</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Managements"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>With Azure Automation, users can easily automate repetitive and time-consuming tasks, often prone to cloud or enterprise setting errors. They can accomplish it using runbooks or desired state configurations for process automation.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Microsoft_SMA_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="Microsoft SMA (software)">Microsoft SMA</a></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Azure_AI">Azure AI</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Azure AI"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>Microsoft Azure Machine Learning (Azure ML) provides tools and frameworks for developers to create their own <a href="/wiki/Machine_learning" title="Machine learning">machine learning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a> (AI) services.</li>
<li>Azure AI Services by Microsoft comprises prebuilt APIs, SDKs, and services developers can customize. These services encompass perceptual and cognitive intelligence features such as <a href="/wiki/Speech_recognition" title="Speech recognition">speech recognition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Speaker_recognition" title="Speaker recognition">speaker recognition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neural_speech_synthesis" class="mw-redirect" title="Neural speech synthesis">neural speech synthesis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Facial_recognition_system" title="Facial recognition system">face recognition</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_vision" title="Computer vision">computer vision</a>, <a href="/wiki/Optical_character_recognition" title="Optical character recognition">OCR</a>/form understanding, <a href="/wiki/Natural_language_processing" title="Natural language processing">natural language processing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machine_translation" title="Machine translation">machine translation</a>, and business decision services. Many AI characteristics in Microsoft's products and services, namely Bing, Office, Teams, Xbox, and Windows, are driven by Azure AI Services.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Azure AI Studio can be used for building and deploying <a href="/wiki/Generative_AI" class="mw-redirect" title="Generative AI">generative AI</a> applications, notably using <a href="/wiki/OpenAI" title="OpenAI">OpenAI</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Foundation_model" title="Foundation model">foundation model</a> <a href="/wiki/GPT-4o" title="GPT-4o">GPT-4o</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Azure_Blockchain_Workbench">Azure Blockchain Workbench</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Azure Blockchain Workbench"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1236090951" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Confidential_Consortium_Framework" title="Confidential Consortium Framework">Confidential Consortium Framework</a></div>
<p>Through Azure<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Blockchain Workbench, Microsoft is providing the required infrastructure to set up a consortium network in multiple topologies using a variety of consensus mechanisms. Microsoft provides integration from these <a href="/wiki/Blockchain" title="Blockchain">blockchain</a> platforms to other Microsoft services to streamline the development of distributed applications. Microsoft supports many general-purpose blockchains, including <a href="/wiki/Ethereum" title="Ethereum">Ethereum</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hyperledger_Fabric" class="mw-redirect" title="Hyperledger Fabric">Hyperledger Fabric</a> and purpose-built blockchains like Corda.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Function">Function</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Function"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Azure functions are used in <a href="/wiki/Serverless_computing" title="Serverless computing">serverless computing</a> architectures, where subscribers can execute code as an event-driven Function-as-a-Service (<a href="/wiki/Function_as_a_service" title="Function as a service">FaaS</a>) without managing the underlying server resources.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Customers using Azure functions are billed based on per-second resource consumption and executions.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Internet_of_Things_(IoT)"><span id="Internet_of_Things_.28IoT.29"></span>Internet of Things (IoT)</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Internet of Things (IoT)"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><b>Azure IoT Hub</b> enables the connection, monitoring, and management of a large number of <a href="/wiki/IoT" class="mw-redirect" title="IoT">IoT</a> assets. On February 4, 2016, Microsoft announced the General Availability of the Azure IoT Hub service.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>Azure IoT Edge</b> is a fully managed service built on IoT Hub that allows for cloud intelligence deployed locally on IoT edge devices.</li>
<li><b>Azure IoT Central</b> is a fully managed <a href="/wiki/SaaS" class="mw-redirect" title="SaaS">SaaS</a> app that makes it easy to connect, monitor, and manage IoT assets at scale.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On December 5, 2017, Microsoft announced the Public Preview of Azure IoT Central, its Azure IoT <a href="/wiki/SaaS" class="mw-redirect" title="SaaS">SaaS</a> service.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On October 4, 2017, Microsoft began shipping GA versions of the official Microsoft Azure IoT Developer Kit (Devkit) board, manufactured by MX Chip.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On April 16, 2018, Microsoft announced the launch of the <a href="/wiki/Azure_Sphere" title="Azure Sphere">Azure Sphere</a>, an end-to-end IoT product that focuses on microcontroller-based devices and uses Linux.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On May 7, 2018, Microsoft announced the launch of <a href="/wiki/Azure_Maps" title="Azure Maps">Azure Maps</a>, an enterprise maps API and SDK platform.</li>
<li>On June 27, 2018, Microsoft launched Azure IoT Edge, used to run Azure services and artificial intelligence on IoT devices.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On November 20, 2018, Microsoft launched the Open Enclave SDK for cross-platform systems such as <a href="/wiki/ARM_architecture#TrustZone" class="mw-redirect" title="ARM architecture">ARM Trust Zone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Intel_SGX" class="mw-redirect" title="Intel SGX">Intel SGX</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Azure_Stack_HCI">Azure Stack HCI</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Azure Stack HCI"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Azure Stack HCI is a <a href="/wiki/Hyper-converged_infrastructure" title="Hyper-converged infrastructure">hyper-converged infrastructure</a> (HCI) product that uses validated hardware to run virtualized workloads on-premises to consolidate aging infrastructure and connect to Azure for cloud services.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Azure_Orbital">Azure Orbital</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Azure Orbital"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Launched in September 2020, Azure Orbital lets private industries and government agencies process satellite data quickly by connecting directly to cloud computing networks. Mobile cloud computing ground stations are also available to provide connectivity to remote locations without ground infrastructure. Third-party satellite systems, like <a href="/wiki/Starlink" title="Starlink">SpaceX's Starlink</a> and <a href="/wiki/O3b" title="O3b">SES' O3b</a> constellation, can be employed.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>SES plans to use Microsoft's data centers to provide cloud connectivity to remote areas through its next generation <a href="/wiki/O3b_mPOWER" title="O3b mPOWER">O3b mPOWER</a> <a href="/wiki/Medium_Earth_orbit" title="Medium Earth orbit">MEO</a> satellites alongside Microsoft's data centers.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The company will deploy satellite control and <a href="/wiki/Transmission_(telecom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Transmission (telecom)">uplink</a> ground stations to achieve this. SES launched the first two O3b mPOWER satellites in December 2022; nine more are scheduled between 2023 and 2024. The service should begin in Q3 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>According to Microsoft, using satellites to connect to cloud data centers may provide faster speeds than complex <a href="/wiki/Fiber-optic_communication" title="Fiber-optic communication">fiber</a> routes. For online media, entertainment, or gaming activities, connecting from home to the cloud can involve longer routes with multiple hops. Through their experiments with Xbox Cloud, Microsoft has discovered that satellite connections are faster than terrestrial networks in certain parts of the world, including specific locations in the USA.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Azure_Container_Storage">Azure Container Storage</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Azure Container Storage"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In August 2024, Azure introduced the industry’s first platform-managed container-native storage solution in the public cloud. This service supports Ephemeral Disks (Local NVMe/Temp SSD) and Azure Disks, offering a robust storage solution tailored for containerized <a href="/wiki/Application_software" title="Application software">applications</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Azure_Quantum">Azure Quantum</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Azure Quantum"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Released for public preview in 2021. <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Azure_Quantum" title="Microsoft Azure Quantum"> Azure Quantum</a> provides access to <a href="/wiki/Quantum_computing" title="Quantum computing">quantum hardware</a> and software.<sup id="cite_ref-ZD_AQ_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZD_AQ-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-TT_AQ_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TT_AQ-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The public <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a> platform includes multiple quantum hardware modalities including trapped ion, neutral atom, and superconducting systems.<sup id="cite_ref-HPC_AQ_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HPC_AQ-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Azure Quantum Elements software for <a href="/wiki/Computational_chemistry" title="Computational chemistry">computational chemistry</a> and materials science combines AI, <a href="/wiki/High-performance_computing" title="High-performance computing">high-performance computing</a> and quantum processors to run molecular simulations and calculations.<sup id="cite_ref-HPC_AQ_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HPC_AQ-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The service includes Copilot, a GPT-4 based <a href="/wiki/Large_language_model" title="Large language model">large language model</a> tool to query and visualize data, write code, and initiate simulations.<sup id="cite_ref-HPC_AQ_63-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HPC_AQ-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2021, Microsoft developed the <a href="/wiki/Quantum_programming" title="Quantum programming">quantum programming</a> language Q# (pronounced <a href="/wiki/Q_Sharp" title="Q Sharp">Q Sharp</a>) and an open-source quantum development kit for algorithm development and simulation.<sup id="cite_ref-ZD_AQ_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZD_AQ-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2023, Microsoft developed Quantum Intermediate Representation (QIR) from <a href="/wiki/LLVM" title="LLVM">LLVM</a> as a common interface between programming languages and target quantum processors.<sup id="cite_ref-IW_AQ_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IW_AQ-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
</p><p>The Azure Quantum Resource Estimator estimates the resources required to execute a given quantum algorithm on a fault-tolerant quantum computer.<sup id="cite_ref-TQI_AQ_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TQI_AQ-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It can also show how future quantum computers will impact today’s encryption algorithms.<sup id="cite_ref-TQI_AQ_65-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TQI_AQ-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Regional_expansion">Regional expansion</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Regional expansion"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>As of 2018, Azure was available in 54 regions,<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and Microsoft was the first primary cloud provider to establish facilities in Africa, with two regions in South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Azure geographies consist of multiple Azure Regions, like "North Europe" (located in Dublin, Ireland) and "West Europe" (located in Amsterdam, Netherlands).
</p><p>On June 19, 2019, Microsoft announced the launch of two new cloud regions in the <a href="/wiki/United_Arab_Emirates" title="United Arab Emirates">United Arab Emirates</a> – Microsoft's first in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On March 6, 2025, the company announced a strategic partnership with the Government of <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, represented by the Central Agency for Information Technology (CAIT) and the <a href="/wiki/Communication_and_Information_Technology_Regulatory_Authority_(Kuwait)" title="Communication and Information Technology Regulatory Authority (Kuwait)">Communication and Information Technology Regulatory Authority (CITRA)</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This collaboration aims to accelerate digital transformation efforts aligned with <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Vision_2035" title="Kuwait Vision 2035">Kuwait’s Vision 2035</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The partnership will focus on creating an AI-powered Azure Region to enhance local <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">AI</a> capabilities, stimulate economic growth, and drive innovation across various industries.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Research_partnerships">Research partnerships</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Research partnerships"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Microsoft has partners that sell its products. In August 2018, <a href="/wiki/Toyota_Tsusho" title="Toyota Tsusho">Toyota Tsusho</a> began a partnership with Microsoft to create <a href="/wiki/Fish_farming" title="Fish farming">fish farming</a> tools using the Microsoft Azure application suite for <a href="/wiki/Internet_of_things" title="Internet of things">IoT</a> technologies related to water management. Developed in part by researchers from <a href="/wiki/Kindai_University" title="Kindai University">Kindai University</a>, the water pump mechanisms use <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a> to count the number of fish on a <a href="/wiki/Conveyor_belt" title="Conveyor belt">conveyor belt</a>, analyze the number of fish, and deduce the effectiveness of water flow from the data the fish provide. The specific <a href="/wiki/Computer_programs" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer programs">computer programs</a> used in the process fall under the Azure Machine Learning and the Azure IoT Hub platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Design">Design</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Design"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Microsoft Azure utilizes a specialized operating system with the same name to power its "fabric layer". This cluster is hosted at Microsoft's data centers and is responsible for managing computing and storage resources and allocating them to applications running on the Microsoft Azure platform. It is a "cloud layer" built upon various Windows Server systems, including the customized Microsoft Azure Hypervisor, which is based on Windows Server 2008 and enables the virtualization of services.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Microsoft Azure Fabric Controller maintains the scalability and dependability of services and environments in the <a href="/wiki/Data_center" title="Data center">data center</a>. It prevents failure in server malfunction and manages users' web applications, including memory allocation and load balancing.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Azure provides an <a href="/wiki/API" title="API">API</a> built on <a href="/wiki/REST" title="REST">REST</a>, <a href="/wiki/HTTP" title="HTTP">HTTP</a>, and <a href="/wiki/XML" title="XML">XML</a> that allows a developer to interact with the services offered by Microsoft Azure. Microsoft also provides a client-side managed class library that encapsulates the functions of interacting with the services. It also integrates with <a href="/wiki/Visual_Studio" title="Visual Studio">Microsoft Visual Studio</a>, <a href="/wiki/Git" title="Git">Git</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Eclipse_(software)" title="Eclipse (software)">Eclipse</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Users can manage Azure services in multiple ways, one of which is through the Web-based Azure Portal, which became generally available in December 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Apart from accessing services via API, users can browse active resources, adjust settings, launch new resources, and view primary monitoring data of functional virtual machines and services using the portal.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Deployment_models">Deployment models</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Deployment models"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Regarding cloud resources, Microsoft Azure offers two deployment models: the "classic" model and the Azure Resource Manager.<sup id="cite_ref-arm_vs_classic_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arm_vs_classic-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In the classic model, each resource, like a virtual machine or SQL database, had to be managed separately, but in 2014,<sup id="cite_ref-arm_vs_classic_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arm_vs_classic-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Azure introduced the Azure Resource Manager, which allows users to group related services. This update makes it easier and more efficient to deploy, manage, and monitor resources that work closely together.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The classic model will eventually be phased out.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Infrastructure_development">Infrastructure development</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Infrastructure development"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In January 2025, Microsoft announced plans to invest $80 billion in AI and data centers as part of its fiscal year 2025 budget. This investment would enhance the scalability and performance of Azure's cloud infrastructure, which supports AI-driven applications, including services developed through Microsoft's partnership with <a href="/wiki/OpenAI" title="OpenAI">OpenAI</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History_and_timeline">History and timeline</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: History and timeline"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Windows_Azure_logo_(2010%E2%80%942012).png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/5/59/Windows_Azure_logo_%282010%E2%80%942012%29.png" decoding="async" width="207" height="26" class="mw-file-element" data-file-width="207" data-file-height="26" /></a><figcaption>Azure logo used from 2010 to 2012, under Windows Azure name</figcaption></figure>
<p>In 2005, Microsoft took over <a href="/wiki/Groove_Networks" title="Groove Networks">Groove Networks</a>, and Bill Gates made Groove's founder <a href="/wiki/Ray_Ozzie" title="Ray Ozzie">Ray Ozzie</a> one of his 5 direct reports as one of 3 chief technology officers. Ozzie met with Amitabh Srivastava, which let Srivastava change course. They convinced <a href="/wiki/Dave_Cutler" title="Dave Cutler">Dave Cutler</a> to postpone his retirement, and their teams developed a cloud operating system.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>October 2008 (<a href="/wiki/Professional_Developers_Conference" title="Professional Developers Conference">PDC</a> LA) – Announced the Windows Azure Platform.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>March 2009 – Announced SQL Azure Relational Database.</li>
<li>November 2009 – Updated Windows Azure CTP, Enabled full trust, PHP, Java, CDN CTP, and more.</li>
<li>February 1, 2010 – Windows Azure Platform commercially available.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>June 2010 – Windows Azure Update, <a href="/wiki/.NET_Framework_4" class="mw-redirect" title=".NET Framework 4">.NET Framework 4</a>, OS Versioning, CDN, SQL Azure Update.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>October 2010 (PDC) – Platform enhancements, Windows Azure Connect, improved Dev / IT Pro Experience.</li>
<li>December 2011 – Traffic manager, SQL Azure reporting, HPC scheduler.</li>
<li>June 2012 – Websites, Virtual machines for Windows and Linux, Python SDK, new portal, locally redundant storage.</li>
<li>April 2014 – Windows Azure renamed Microsoft Azure,<sup id="cite_ref-renaming_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-renaming-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> ARM Portal introduced at Build 2014.</li>
<li>July 2014 – Azure Machine Learning public preview.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>November 2014 – Outage affecting major websites, including MSN.com.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>September 2015 – Azure Cloud Switch introduced as a cross-platform Linux distribution. Currently known as <a href="/wiki/SONiC_(operating_system)" title="SONiC (operating system)">SONiC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>December 2015 – Azure ARM Portal (codename "Ibiza") released.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>March 2016 – Azure Service Fabric is Generally Available (GA).<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>November 15, 2016 – Azure Functions is Generally Available (GA).<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>May 10, 2017 – Azure Cosmos DB is Generally Available (GA).<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>May 7, 2018 – Azure Maps is Generally Available (GA).<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>July 16, 2018 – Azure Service Fabric Mesh public preview.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>September 24, 2018 – Microsoft Azure IoT Central is Generally Available (GA).<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>October 10, 2018 – Microsoft joins the <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux-oriented</a> group <a href="/wiki/Open_Invention_Network" title="Open Invention Network">Open Invention Network</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>April 17, 2019 – Azure Front Door Service is now available.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>March 2020 – Microsoft said that there was a 775% increase in <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Teams" title="Microsoft Teams">Microsoft Teams</a> usage in Italy due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>. The company estimates there are now 44 million daily active users of Teams worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>January 17, 2023 – Azure OpenAI Service is Generally Available (GA).<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Privacy">Privacy</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Privacy"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>According to the <a href="/wiki/Patriot_Act" title="Patriot Act">Patriot Act</a>, Microsoft has acknowledged that the U.S. government can access data even if the hosting company is not American and the data is outside the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> To address concerns related to privacy and security, Microsoft has established the Microsoft Azure Trust Center.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Microsoft Azure offers services that comply with multiple compliance programs, including <a href="/wiki/ISO_27001:2005" class="mw-redirect" title="ISO 27001:2005">ISO 27001:2005</a> and <a href="/wiki/HIPAA" class="mw-redirect" title="HIPAA">HIPAA</a>. A comprehensive and up-to-date list of these services is available on the Microsoft Azure Trust Center Compliance page.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Microsoft Azure received JAB Provisional Authority to Operate (P-ATO) from the U.S. government under the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Risk_and_Authorization_Management_Program" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Risk and Authorization Management Program">Federal Risk and Authorization Management Program (FedRAMP)</a> guidelines. This program provides a standardized approach to security assessment, authorization, and continuous monitoring for cloud services used by the federal government.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Certifications">Certifications</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Certifications"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>A large variety of Azure certifications can be attained, each requiring one or multiple successfully completed examinations. Certification levels range from beginner, intermediate to expert.
</p><p><b>Examples of common certifications include:</b>
</p>
<ul><li>Azure Fundamentals</li>
<li>Azure Data Fundamentals</li>
<li>Azure AI Engineer Associate</li>
<li>Azure AI Fundamentals</li>
<li>Azure Cosmos DB Developer Specialty</li>
<li>Azure Administrator Associate</li>
<li>Azure Data Engineer Associate</li>
<li>Azure Data Scientist Associate</li>
<li>Azure Database Administrator Associate</li>
<li>Azure Developer Associate</li>
<li>Azure Enterprise Data Analyst Associate</li>
<li>Azure Security Engineer Associate</li>
<li>Azure Security Operations Analyst Associate</li>
<li>Azure Identity and Access Administrator Associate</li>
<li>Azure Security, Compliance, and Identity Fundamentals</li>
<li>Azure Network Engineer Associate</li>
<li>Azure Windows Server Hybrid Administrator Associate</li>
<li>Azure Virtual Desktop Specialty</li>
<li>Azure for SAP Workloads Specialty</li>
<li>Azure Customer Data Platform Specialty</li>
<li>Azure Cybersecurity Architect Expert</li>
<li>Azure Solutions Architect Expert</li>
<li>Azure Power Platform Solution Architect Expert</li>
<li>Azure DevOps Engineer Expert</li>
<li>Azure IoT Developer Specialty</li>
<li>Azure Stack Hub Operator Associate</li>
<li>Azure Machine Learning Specialty</li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Key_people">Key people</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Key people"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dave_Cutler" title="Dave Cutler">Dave Cutler</a>, Lead Developer, Microsoft Azure<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mark_Russinovich" title="Mark Russinovich">Mark Russinovich</a>, CTO, Microsoft Azure<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Scott_Guthrie" title="Scott Guthrie">Scott Guthrie</a>, Executive Vice President of the Cloud and AI group in Microsoft</li>
<li>Jason Zander, Executive Vice President, Microsoft Azure<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Julia White, Corporate Vice President, Microsoft Azure<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Issues">Issues</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Issues"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Microsoft Azure's services can have varied and complex pricing models. <sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Azure Portal can be slow and prone to user errors. <sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Security">Security</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Microsoft_Azure&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Security"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In August 2021, researchers from <a href="/wiki/Wiz_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wiz (company)">Wiz Research</a> claimed to have discovered a vulnerability in the Azure <a href="/wiki/Cosmos_DB" title="Cosmos DB">Cosmos DB</a> database, referred to as "ChaosDB." They claimed that they had gained complete unrestricted access to the accounts and databases of several thousand Microsoft Azure customers. <sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In August 2021, Microsoft claimed they mitigated the vulnerability and no customer data was accessed. <sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2021, researchers from <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto_Networks" title="Palo Alto Networks">Palo Alto Networks</a> claimed to discover a significant cross-account takeover <a href="/wiki/Vulnerability_(computer_security)" title="Vulnerability (computer security)">vulnerability</a> in Azure Container Instances, named "Azurescape". According to Palo Alto Networks' researchers, this vulnerability is the first known instance that allows one user of a public cloud service to escape their environment and execute code on other users' environments within the same service. Although Microsoft quickly patched the issue, Palo Alto Networks advised Azure customers to revoke any privileged credentials deployed before August 31, 2021, as a precaution. <sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In September 2021, Microsoft claimed they fixed the vulnerability. <sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In September 2021, researchers from <a href="/wiki/Wiz_(company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wiz (company)">Wiz Research</a> claimed they found four critical vulnerabilities in the Open Management Infrastructure (OMI), which is Azure's software agent deployed on a large portion of <a href="/wiki/Linux" title="Linux">Linux</a> <a href="/wiki/Virtual_machine" title="Virtual machine">VMs</a> in Azure. The researchers named it "OMIGOD" and claimed that these vulnerabilities allowed for <a href="/wiki/Arbitrary_code_execution" title="Arbitrary code execution">remote code execution</a> within the Azure network and could escalate privileges to root. They claimed that the vulnerabilities affected various Azure services, including Azure Log Analytics, Azure Diagnostics, and Azure Security Center. <sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In response, Microsoft announced that it had released fixes for the aforementioned vulnerabilities in September 2021. <sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In July 2023, U.S. Senator <a href="/wiki/Ron_Wyden" title="Ron Wyden">Ron Wyden</a> called on the <a href="/wiki/Cybersecurity_and_Infrastructure_Security_Agency" title="Cybersecurity and Infrastructure Security Agency">Cybersecurity and Infrastructure Security Agency</a> (CISA), the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">Justice Department</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Trade_Commission" title="Federal Trade Commission">Federal Trade Commission</a> to hold Microsoft accountable for what he described as "negligent cybersecurity practices." This came in the wake of an alleged cyberattack orchestrated by Chinese hackers, who exploited a vulnerability in Microsoft's software to compromise U.S. government email systems.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Similarly, <a href="/wiki/Amit_Yoran" title="Amit Yoran">Amit Yoran</a>, the CEO of cybersecurity firm <a href="/wiki/Tenable,_Inc." title="Tenable, Inc.">Tenable, Inc.</a>, lambasted Microsoft for what he termed "grossly irresponsible" actions, accusing the company of fostering a "culture of toxic obfuscation."<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cyber_Safety_Review_Board" title="Cyber Safety Review Board">Cyber Safety Review Board</a> produced a report that blamed Microsoft about a cascade of security failures that allowed the intrusion to succeed. Microsoft's security culture was called inadequate.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
